## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive equation relating stress to strain and temperature, a fundamental problem in materials science where temperature-dependent mechanical behavior involves elastic moduli, yield stress, strain hardening, and thermal softening effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal modulus correction)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (elastic-plastic with hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (coupled power-law in strain and temperature)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturation hardening with temperature dependence)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 - c2 * T) (linear elastic-plastic with thermal softening factor)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation in deformation)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening with pre-strain)
- Swift with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power-law with thermal activation)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 + c3 * T (polynomial stress-strain with temperature offset)
- Hyperbolic sine creep: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo-type thermally activated flow)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (T/T_ref)**(-c) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition → σ = f(ε) × g(T) separating strain hardening from thermal softening as independent multiplicative contributions
- Pre-strain offset → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to avoid singularity at zero strain and model initial yield
- Thermally activated deformation → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting Arrhenius-type thermal activation of dislocation motion
- Concave-up vs concave-down strain response → power exponent n<1 gives concave-down (hardening saturation), n>1 gives concave-up (accelerating hardening)
- Phase transition or softening discontinuity → tanh(c*(T - T_critical)) to model abrupt property changes at critical temperatures
- Linear elastic regime dominance → at small strains, sigma ≈ c0*epsilon should dominate regardless of hardening model
